  > Total Learning AI Types ≈ 80–100
  > 
  > Next logical domain:
  > 
  > Domain 3 — Reasoning AI (Chain of Thought, Tree of Thought, ReAct, Reflection, Debate, Constitutional AI, Neuro-Symbolic AI, Causal AI, Graph Reasoning, Multi-Agent Reasoning, etc.). This is one of the most important domains for Agentic AI and enterprise decision-making.Domain 3 — Reasoning AI
  > 
  > This is the domain most people confuse with LLMs.
  > 
  > An LLM generates text.
  > 
  > Reasoning AI thinks before acting.
  > 
  > This domain powers:
  > 
  > Agentic AI
  > Autonomous Systems
  > Decision Intelligence
  > AI Architects
  > AI Analysts
  > AI Managers
  > AI Control Towers
  > Reasoning AI Architecture
  > Reasoning AI
  > │
  > ├── Logical Reasoning
  > ├── Symbolic Reasoning
  > ├── Causal Reasoning
  > ├── Probabilistic Reasoning
  > ├── Mathematical Reasoning
  > ├── Multi-Step Reasoning
  > ├── Planning Reasoning
  > ├── Graph Reasoning
  > ├── Scientific Reasoning
  > ├── Legal Reasoning
  > ├── Financial Reasoning
  > ├── Multi-Agent Reasoning
  > ├── Self-Reflection Reasoning
  > └── Autonomous Reasoning
  > A. Logical Reasoning AI
  > 
  > Foundation of decision making.
  > 
  > AI Type	Purpose
  > Deductive Reasoning	General → Specific
  > Inductive Reasoning	Specific → General
  > Abductive Reasoning	Best Explanation
  > Rule-Based Reasoning	Business Rules
  > Constraint Reasoning	Boundaries
  > Policy Reasoning	Policies
  > 
  > Insurance Example:
  > 
  > Customer Age <18
  > 
  > Policy Restriction
  > 
  > Reject Claim
  > B. Symbolic Reasoning AI
  > 
  > Uses explicit rules.
  > 
  > AI Type
  > Expert Systems
  > Rule Engines
  > Knowledge Rules
  > Ontology Reasoning
  > Semantic Reasoning
  > Business Rule AI
  > 
  > Tools often used:
  > 
  > Drools
  > Open Policy Agent
  > 
  > Insurance Example:
  > 
  > Coverage rules.
  > 
  > C. Causal Reasoning AI
  > 
  > Most organizations only do correlation.
  > 
  > Top companies do causation.
  > 
  > AI Type
  > Cause Effect Reasoning
  > Root Cause Analysis
  > Counterfactual Reasoning
  > Structural Causal Models
  > Intervention Analysis
  > 
  > Questions:
  > 
  > Why did fraud increase?
  > Why did claims spike?
  > D. Probabilistic Reasoning AI
  > 
  > Works with uncertainty.
  > 
  > AI Type
  > Bayesian Reasoning
  > Probabilistic Graphs
  > Belief Networks
  > Markov Models
  > Hidden Markov Models
  > 
  > Insurance Example:
  > 
  > Accident Report
  > 
  > ↓
  > 
  > 80% Fraud Probability
  > 
  > ↓
  > 
  > Investigate
  > E. Mathematical Reasoning AI
  > AI Type
  > Arithmetic Reasoning
  > Statistical Reasoning
  > Optimization Reasoning
  > Quantitative Reasoning
  > Financial Reasoning
  > 
  > Insurance Example:
  > 
  > Premium calculations.
  > 
  > F. Multi-Step Reasoning AI
  > 
  > Enterprise agents use this heavily.
  > 
  > AI Type
  > Chain of Thought (CoT)
  > Self Consistency
  > Program of Thought
  > Step-by-Step Reasoning
  > Scratchpad Reasoning
  > 
  > Example:
  > 
  > Claim
  > 
  > ↓
  > 
  > Coverage Check
  > 
  > ↓
  > 
  > Fraud Check
  > 
  > ↓
  > 
  > Risk Score
  > 
  > ↓
  > 
  > Settlement
  > G. Tree-Based Reasoning
  > 
  > Explores alternatives.
  > 
  > AI Type
  > Tree of Thoughts
  > Search Tree Reasoning
  > Branch Exploration
  > Decision Tree Reasoning
  > 
  > Example:
  > 
  > Approve
  > 
  > Investigate
  > 
  > Reject
  > 
  > Escalate
  > 
  > AI evaluates all branches.
  > 
  > H. Graph Reasoning
  > 
  > Critical for GraphRAG.
  > 
  > AI Type
  > Graph Traversal Reasoning
  > Relationship Reasoning
  > Knowledge Graph Reasoning
  > Entity Reasoning
  > Path Reasoning
  > 
  > Insurance Example:
  > 
  > Claimant
  > 
  > ↓
  > 
  > Repair Shop
  > 
  > ↓
  > 
  > Witness
  > 
  > ↓
  > 
  > Previous Fraud Ring
  > I. ReAct Reasoning
  > 
  > Reason + Act.
  > 
  > Very common in agents.
  > 
  > AI Type
  > ReAct
  > Tool Reasoning
  > Action Planning
  > Tool Selection
  > 
  > Example:
  > 
  > Think
  > 
  > ↓
  > 
  > Search
  > 
  > ↓
  > 
  > Analyze
  > 
  > ↓
  > 
  > Act
  > J. Reflection AI
  > 
  > AI reviews itself.
  > 
  > AI Type
  > Reflection
  > Self Critique
  > Self Correction
  > Self Review
  > Self Improvement
  > 
  > Example:
  > 
  > Generate
  > 
  > ↓
  > 
  > Review
  > 
  > ↓
  > 
  > Improve
  > 
  > ↓
  > 
  > Return
  > K. Debate AI
  > 
  > Multiple agents debate.
  > 
  > AI Type
  > Debate Reasoning
  > Adversarial Reasoning
  > Multi-Agent Debate
  > Consensus Reasoning
  > 
  > Insurance Example:
  > 
  > Fraud Agent
  > 
  > vs
  > 
  > Claims Agent
  > 
  > vs
  > 
  > Legal Agent
  > L. Constitutional AI
  > 
  > Policy-driven reasoning.
  > 
  > Associated with:
  > 
  > Anthropic
  > AI Type
  > Constitutional Reasoning
  > Ethical Reasoning
  > Safety Reasoning
  > Policy Compliance Reasoning
  > M. Scientific Reasoning
  > 
  > Used in healthcare and research.
  > 
  > AI Type
  > Hypothesis Reasoning
  > Experiment Reasoning
  > Clinical Reasoning
  > Research Reasoning
  > 
  > Your EEG/DBA work fits here.
  > 
  > N. Legal Reasoning
  > AI Type
  > Contract Reasoning
  > Regulatory Reasoning
  > Compliance Reasoning
  > Policy Interpretation
  > 
  > Insurance heavily uses this.
  > 
  > O. Financial Reasoning
  > AI Type
  > Risk Reasoning
  > Investment Reasoning
  > Credit Reasoning
  > Pricing Reasoning
  > P. Strategic Reasoning
  > 
  > Used by AI Managers.
  > 
  > AI Type
  > Strategic Planning
  > Business Reasoning
  > Portfolio Reasoning
  > Resource Reasoning
  > Q. Multi-Agent Reasoning
  > 
  > Agent ecosystems.
  > 
  > AI Type
  > Agent Collaboration
  > Agent Negotiation
  > Agent Voting
  > Agent Consensus
  > Agent Arbitration
  > 
  > Example:
  > 
  > Planner Agent
  > 
  > ↓
  > 
  > Architect Agent
  > 
  > ↓
  > 
  > Developer Agent
  > 
  > ↓
  > 
  > QA Agent
  > 
  > ↓
  > 
  > Security Agent
  > R. Neuro-Symbolic Reasoning
  > 
  > One of the most important future domains.
  > 
  > Combines:
  > 
  > Neural Networks
  > +
  > Rules
  > +
  > Knowledge Graphs
  > AI Type
  > Neuro-Symbolic AI
  > Hybrid Reasoning
  > Explainable Reasoning
  > Structured Reasoning
  > S. Autonomous Reasoning
  > 
  > Future frontier.
  > 
  > AI Type
  > Self-Directed Reasoning
  > Self-Improving Reasoning
  > Recursive Reasoning
  > Recursive Self-Improvement
  > Insurance Claims Mapping
  > Process	Reasoning Type
  > Fraud Detection	Causal Reasoning
  > Claim Approval	Rule Reasoning
  > Coverage Validation	Legal Reasoning
  > Settlement	Financial Reasoning
  > Escalation	Decision Reasoning
  > Investigation	Graph Reasoning
  > Audit	Compliance Reasoning
  > Auto-Adjudication	Autonomous Reasoning
  > Domain 3 Summary
  > Area	Count
  > Logical Reasoning	10+
  > Symbolic Reasoning	10+
  > Causal Reasoning	10+
  > Probabilistic Reasoning	10+
  > Multi-Step Reasoning	10+
  > Reflection & Debate	10+
  > Graph Reasoning	10+
  > Strategic Reasoning	10+
  > Multi-Agent Reasoning	10+
  > Neuro-Symbolic Reasoning	10+
  > Total Reasoning AI Types
  > 
  > ~100+ reasoning capabilities
  > 
  > Dependency Flow
  > Learning AI
  >       ↓
  > Reasoning AI
  >       ↓
  > Planning AI
  >       ↓
  > Decision AI
  >       ↓
  > Agentic AI
  >       ↓
  > Autonomous AI
  > 
  > The next domain should be:
  > 
  > Domain 4 — Planning AI, which includes goal decomposition, task planning, workflow planning, hierarchical planning, dynamic planning, temporal planning, strategic planning, agent planning, orchestration planning, and autonomous execution planning. This domain is the bridge between Reasoning AI and Agentic AI.Domain 4 — Planning AI
  > 
  > This is where AI moves from:
  > 
  > Thinking
  >    ↓
  > Planning
  >    ↓
  > Executing
  > 
  > Most enterprise AI projects fail because they have:
  > 
  > LLM ✓
  > RAG ✓
  > Agents ✓
  > 
  > But no planning layer.
  > 
  > Without Planning AI:
  > 
  > Smart AI
  > +
  > No Plan
  > =
  > Random Behavior
  > Planning AI Architecture
  > Planning AI
  > │
  > ├── Goal Planning
  > ├── Task Planning
  > ├── Workflow Planning
  > ├── Strategic Planning
  > ├── Tactical Planning
  > ├── Operational Planning
  > ├── Resource Planning
  > ├── Scheduling Planning
  > ├── Agent Planning
  > ├── Multi-Agent Planning
  > ├── Adaptive Planning
  > ├── Dynamic Planning
  > ├── Autonomous Planning
  > └── Execution Planning
  > A. Goal Planning AI
  > 
  > Determines:
  > 
  > What am I trying to achieve?
  > AI Type	Purpose
  > Goal Planning	Define objective
  > Goal Prioritization	Rank goals
  > Goal Optimization	Best path
  > Goal Validation	Verify goals
  > Goal Tracking	Monitor progress
  > 
  > Insurance Example:
  > 
  > Goal
  > 
  > Reduce Claim Processing
  > 
  > 10 Days
  > 
  > ↓
  > 
  > 2 Days
  > B. Task Planning AI
  > 
  > Breaks goals into tasks.
  > 
  > AI Type
  > Task Decomposition
  > Task Sequencing
  > Task Dependency Planning
  > Task Prioritization
  > Task Allocation
  > 
  > Example:
  > 
  > Claim Processing
  > 
  > ↓
  > 
  > Document Review
  > 
  > ↓
  > 
  > Fraud Check
  > 
  > ↓
  > 
  > Coverage Validation
  > 
  > ↓
  > 
  > Settlement
  > C. Workflow Planning AI
  > 
  > Designs end-to-end process.
  > 
  > AI Type
  > Workflow Planning
  > BPM Planning
  > Process Planning
  > Event Planning
  > Workflow Optimization
  > 
  > Example:
  > 
  > FNOL
  > 
  > ↓
  > 
  > Review
  > 
  > ↓
  > 
  > Fraud
  > 
  > ↓
  > 
  > Approval
  > 
  > ↓
  > 
  > Payment
  > D. Strategic Planning AI
  > 
  > Executive-level planning.
  > 
  > AI Type
  > Corporate Planning
  > Business Planning
  > Portfolio Planning
  > Transformation Planning
  > Enterprise Planning
  > 
  > Insurance Example:
  > 
  > Increase Claims Automation
  > 
  > 20%
  > 
  > ↓
  > 
  > 80%
  > E. Tactical Planning AI
  > 
  > Department-level planning.
  > 
  > AI Type
  > Department Planning
  > Program Planning
  > Team Planning
  > Capacity Planning
  > Resource Planning
  > 
  > Example:
  > 
  > Claims Department Roadmap.
  > 
  > F. Operational Planning AI
  > 
  > Day-to-day execution.

  > Work Allocation
  > Resource Assignment
  > Queue Management
  > 
  > Insurance Example:
  > 
  > Assign claims to adjusters.
  > 
  > G. Scheduling Planning AI
  > 
  > Time-based planning.

  > Resource Scheduling
  > Workforce Scheduling
  > Appointment Planning
  > 
  > Insurance Example:
  > 
  > Inspection scheduling.
  > 
  > H. Resource Planning AI
  > 
  > Optimizes resources.
  > 
  > AI Type
  > Human Resource Planning
  > Agent Resource Planning
  > GPU Planning
  > Budget Planning
  > Infrastructure Planning
  > 
  > Example:
  > 
  > Claims Volume ↑
  > 
  > ↓
  > 
  > Add AI Agents
  > 
  > ↓
  > 
  > Reduce Backlog
  > I. Dependency Planning AI
  > 
  > Understands relationships.
  > 
  > AI Type
  > Dependency Planning
  > Critical Path Planning
  > Constraint Planning
  > Requirement Planning
  > 
  > Example:
  > 
  > Fraud Check
  > 
  > Must Complete
  > 
  > Before
  > 
  > Settlement
  > J. Hierarchical Planning AI
  > 
  > Large goal → smaller goals.
  > 
  > AI Type
  > Hierarchical Planning
  > Recursive Planning
  > Tree Planning
  > Layered Planning
  > 
  > Example:
  > 
  > Claims Department
  > 
  > ↓
  > 
  > Fraud
  > 
  > ↓
  > 
  > Investigation
  > 
  > ↓
  > 
  > Settlement
  > K. Dynamic Planning AI
  > 
  > Changes plan in real time.
  >

  > Real-Time Planning
  > Event Driven Planning
  > 
  > Insurance Example:
  > 
  > Fraud Found
  > 
  > ↓
  > 
  > Change Workflow
  > 
  > ↓
  > 
  > Investigation Path
  > L. Agent Planning AI

  > AI creates plans itself.

  >

  > Dependency Chain
  > Learning AI
  >       ↓
  > Reasoning AI
  >       ↓
  > Planning AI
  >       ↓
  > Memory AI
  >       ↓
  > Knowledge AI
  >       ↓
  > Decision AI
  >       ↓
  > Agentic AI
  >       ↓
  > Autonomous AI
  > 
  > The next domain should be Domain 5 — Memory AI, one of the most overlooked domains in enterprise AI. It covers episodic memory, semantic memory, procedural memory, vector memory, graph memory, agent memory, organizational memory, shared memory, long-term memory, and memory governance. This is what makes agents improve over time instead of forgetting everything after each session.Domain 5 — Memory AI
  > 
  > This is one of the most misunderstood domains.
  > 
  > Most companies think:
  > 
  > Chat History = Memory
  > 
  > Wrong.
  > 
  > A real enterprise AI system has multiple memory layers, similar to the human brain.
  > 
  > Without Memory AI:
  > 
  > LLM
  >  ↓
  > Answer
  >  ↓
  > Forget
  > 
  > With Memory AI:
  > 
  > Learn
  >  ↓
  > Remember
  >  ↓
  > Improve
  >  ↓
  > Reuse
  > Memory AI Architecture
  > Memory AI
  > │
  > ├── Working Memory
  > ├── Short-Term Memory
  > ├── Long-Term Memory
  > ├── Episodic Memory
  > ├── Semantic Memory
  > ├── Procedural Memory
  > ├── Agent Memory
  > ├── Team Memory
  > ├── Organizational Memory
  > ├── Shared Memory
  > ├── Vector Memory
  > ├── Graph Memory
  > ├── Retrieval Memory
  > ├── Temporal Memory
  > ├── Personal Memory
  > ├── Business Memory
  > ├── Decision Memory
  > ├── Experience Memory
  > └── Autonomous Memory
  > A. Working Memory
  > 
  > Current task memory.
  > 
  > Equivalent:
  > 
  > Human Brain
  > =
  > Current Thought
  > 
  > Examples:
  > 
  > Current conversation
  > Current workflow
  > Current claim
  > 
  > AI Types:
  > 
  > Type
  > Session Memory
  > Context Memory
  > Runtime Memory
  > Active Memory
  > Conversation Memory
  > 
  > Insurance Example:
  > 
  > Claim #12345
  > 
  > Customer Name
  > 
  > Policy Details
  > 
  > Current Status
  > 
  > Only needed during processing.
  > 
  > B. Short-Term Memory
  > 
  > Stores recent events.
  > 
  > Examples:
  > 
  > Last 10 conversations
  > Last 100 claims
  > Recent actions
  > 
  > AI Types:
  > 
  > Type
  > Recent Memory
  > Interaction Memory
  > Session History
  > Context Window Memory
  > C. Long-Term Memory
  > 
  > Stores information for years.
  > 
  > Examples:
  > 
  > Customer history
  > Policy history
  > Claim history
  > 
  > AI Types:
  > 
  > Type
  > Persistent Memory
  > Historical Memory
  > Enterprise Memory
  > Archival Memory
  > D. Episodic Memory
  > 
  > Stores experiences.
  > 
  > Human Example:
  > 
  > I remember my vacation.
  > 
  > AI Example:
  > 
  > Claim Investigation #2045
  > 
  > Fraud Detected
  > 
  > Successful Outcome
  > 
  > AI Types:
  > 
  > Type
  > Experience Memory
  > Event Memory
  > Incident Memory
  > Workflow Memory
  > E. Semantic Memory
  > 
  > Stores facts.
  > 
  > Human Example:
  > 
  > Calgary is in Alberta.
  > 
  > AI Example:
  > 
  > Policy ABC Covers Hail Damage
  > 
  > AI Types:
  > 
  > Type
  > Knowledge Memory
  > Fact Memory
  > Reference Memory
  > Enterprise Knowledge Memory
  > F. Procedural Memory
  > 
  > Stores how to do something.
  > 
  > Human Example:
  > 
  > Driving a car
  > 
  > AI Example:
  > 
  > How to Process a Claim
  > 
  > AI Types:
  > 
  > Type
  > Workflow Memory
  > SOP Memory
  > Process Memory
  > Operational Memory
  > G. Vector Memory
  > 
  > Most common in GenAI.
  > 
  > Stored in:
  > 
  > Vector DB
  > 
  > Examples:
  > 
  > Embeddings
  > Semantic Similarity
  > 
  > Technologies:
  > 
  > Pinecone
  > Qdrant
  > Weaviate
  > 
  > AI Types:
  > 
  > Type
  > Embedding Memory
  > Similarity Memory
  > Semantic Memory Store
  > H. Graph Memory
  > 
  > Stores relationships.
  > 
  > Example:
  > 
  > Customer
  > 
  > ↓
  > 
  > Vehicle
  > 
  > ↓
  > 
  > Claim
  > 
  > ↓
  > 
  > Repair Shop
  > 
  > ↓
  > 
  > Fraud Ring
  > 
  > Technologies:
  > 
  > Neo4j
  > 
  > AI Types:
  > 
  > Type
  > Relationship Memory
  > Knowledge Graph Memory
  > Network Memory
  > I. Agent Memory
  > 
  > Specific to agents.
  > 
  > Examples:
  > 
  > Previous tasks
  > Tool usage
  > Success rate
  > 
  > AI Types:
  > 
  > Type
  > Planner Memory
  > Agent State Memory
  > Agent History Memory
  > Agent Learning Memory
  > J. Shared Memory
  > 
  > Many agents share.
  > 
  > Example:

  > 
  > ↓
  > 
  > Shared Memory
  > 
  > ↑
  >

  > K. Organizational Memory
  > 
  > Stores company knowledge.

  > Examples:

  > Policies
  > SOPs
  > Regulations
  > Historical decisions
  > 
  > AI Types:
  > 
  > Type
  > Enterprise Memory
  > Corporate Memory
  > Department Memory
  > L. Temporal Memory
  > 
  > Time-aware memory.
  > 
  > Example:
  > 
  > 2024 Policy
  > 
  > Different from
  > 
  > 2026 Policy
  > 
  > AI Types:
  > 
  > Type
  > Timeline Memory
  > Historical Memory
  > Event Sequence Memory
  > M. Personal Memory
  > 
  > Customer specific.
  > 
  > Example:
  > 
  > Customer
  > 
  > Preferred Contact
  > 
  > Claim History
  > 
  > Risk Score
  > 
  > AI Types:
  > 
  > Type
  > User Memory
  > Customer Memory
  > Profile Memory
  > N. Business Memory
  > 
  > Stores enterprise operations.
  > 
  > Examples:
  > 
  > KPIs
  > Metrics
  > Risks
  > Decisions
  > 
  > AI Types:
  > 
  > Type
  > Operational Memory
  > Business Memory
  > KPI Memory
  > O. Decision Memory
  > 
  > Stores decisions.
  > 
  > Example:
  > 
  > Claim Rejected
  > 
  > Reason:
  > 
  > Fraud Detected
  > 
  > AI Types:
  > 
  > Type
  > Decision History
  > Approval Memory
  > Governance Memory
  > P. Experience Memory
  > 
  > Used for learning.
  > 
  > Example:
  > 
  > 1000 Fraud Cases
  > 
  > ↓
  > 
  > Learn Patterns
  > 
  > ↓

  > Reuse Patterns
  > 
  > AI Types:
  > 
  > Type
  > Experience Repository
  > Pattern Memory
  > Learning Memory
  > Q. Retrieval Memory
  > 
  > Supports RAG.
  > 
  > Examples:
  > 
  > Previous retrievals
  > Search history
  > Query patterns
  > 
  > AI Types:
  > 
  > Type
  > Retrieval Cache
  > Search Memory
  > Query Memory
  > R. Autonomous Memory
  > 
  > Future architecture.
  > 
  > AI decides:
  > 
  > What to Remember
  > 
  > What to Forget
  > 
  > What to Compress
  > 
  > AI Types:
  > 
  > Type
  > Self-Managing Memory
  > Adaptive Memory
  > Memory Optimization
  > Recursive Memory
  > Memory Governance AI
  > 
  > Often forgotten.
  > 
  > Questions:
  > 
  > What should be retained?
  > How long?
  > GDPR deletion?
  > PII masking?
  > 
  > AI Types:
  > 
  > Type
  > Memory Governance
  > Memory Compliance
  > Retention Management
  > Memory Audit
  > Insurance Claims Example
  > Claim Arrives
  > 
  > ↓
  > 
  > Working Memory

  > Memory AI Technology Mapping
  > Memory Type	Technology
  > Working Memory	Redis
  > Session Memory	Redis
  > Episodic Memory	PostgreSQL
  > Semantic Memory	Vector DB
  > Graph Memory	Neo4j

  > Shared Memory	Redis Cluster
  > Organizational Memory	Knowledge Graph
  > Decision Memory	Audit Store
  > Experience Memory	Learning Repository

  > Autonomous AI
  > 
  > The next domain should be Domain 6 — Knowledge AI, covering ontology, taxonomy, knowledge graphs, semantic layers, enterprise knowledge, master data intelligence, metadata intelligence, graph intelligence, and enterprise memory-to-knowledge transformation. This becomes the foundation of GraphRAG and enterprise AI operating systems.Domain 6 — Knowledge AI
  > 
  > This is the domain that separates a chatbot from an enterprise AI system.
  > 
  > Most organizations have:
  > 
  > Documents
  > PDFs
  > Emails
  > Spreadsheets
  > Databases
  > 
  > But they don't have:
  > 
  > Knowledge
  > Meaning
  > Relationships
  > Business Context
  > Enterprise Intelligence
  > 
  > Knowledge AI converts data and information into reusable enterprise knowledge.
  > 
  > Knowledge AI Architecture
  > Knowledge AI
  > │
  > ├── Knowledge Management
  > ├── Knowledge Representation
  > ├── Knowledge Graph
  > ├── Ontology Management
  > ├── Taxonomy Management
  > ├── Semantic Intelligence
  > ├── Metadata Intelligence
  > ├── Master Data Intelligence
  > ├── Relationship Intelligence
  > ├── Enterprise Knowledge
  > ├── Domain Knowledge
  > ├── Expert Knowledge
  > ├── Knowledge Discovery
  > ├── Knowledge Reasoning
  > ├── Knowledge Governance
  > └── Knowledge Automation
  > A. Knowledge Management AI
  > 
  > Stores and manages enterprise knowledge.
  > 
  > AI Type	Purpose
  > Knowledge Management AI	Enterprise knowledge
  > Enterprise Knowledge AI	Corporate intelligence
  > Knowledge Repository AI	Central repository
  > Knowledge Lifecycle AI	Knowledge maintenance
  > Knowledge Automation AI	Auto updates
  > 
  > Insurance Example:
  > 
  > Policy Documents
  > Claims Manuals
  > Regulations
  > Procedures
  > B. Knowledge Representation AI
  > 
  > How AI understands knowledge.

  > Knowledge Representation
  > Concept Modeling
  > Semantic Representation
  > Entity Modeling
  > Relationship Modeling

  > 
  > Customer

  > Policy
  > Covers
  > Vehicle
  > C. Ontology AI
  >

  > What is a Policy?
  > What is a Claim?
